Paul Jacobson: Executive VP & CFO Yes. Just to add to that, Dan, I think as we went through the restructuring, we were mindful of where is the excess capacity that we know we're not going to need for a long time because we had built up for a very different regulatory environment, as Mary had said. But we're also cognizant of making sure that we preserve capacity to be able to pivot and rotate where we need to, to get the cost savings. So particularly as it relates to battery capacity, we've got enough to be able to transition to LMR and to LFP as those projects get underway over the next couple of years. So it really was trying to look at what is the right short-term decision, but also how do we balance that against the long term and where we know it's going to go or we believe it's going to go in the future. Paul Jacobson: Executive VP & CFO Yes. Thanks, Itay. Obviously, we're really excited about the new trucks that are coming online. We'll obviously have to take some downtime as we retool for that. On the pricing, I would say it's largely going to be a 2027 tailwind, I think, going forward. And the one thing I've shared this with a number of investors that the historical norm of a giant up in price for a model year really doesn't hold in this environment where pricing has held up on the later years of the model run going forward. So obviously, in the low inventory, low incentive world that we've seen, we haven't seen the typical pricing heuristic where we see a lot of pricing erosion at the end of a production run. Paul Jacobson: Executive VP & CFO Yes. So Colin, thanks for the question. So we tried to do a good job of laying out sort of the key headwinds and tailwinds. But when we lay all of that out together, we actually see some upside coming through on that. Some of it will be in our ability to lower our net tariff exposure. Some of it will be on the regulatory side that we expect coming in as well. And then some of it is going to be continued work on driving EV profitability improvement. Paul Jacobson: Executive VP & CFO Yes. So all of this starts, Emmanuel, with what we see on the monthly cash and where we see the exposure. Paul Jacobson: Executive VP & CFO Yes, Ryan, obviously, the compliance requirements are pretty complicated. You've got both state, federal, local and international as well. But as we've talked about, the credits were roughly split between CAFE and GHG. So CAFE, we know we don't need to purchase credits as the administration has already zeroed out the CAFE penalties across the board. We took a charge for that in the third quarter and expect that to result in some year-over-year savings in '26 versus '25. And then GHG is still pending with the administration. We're assuming that ultimately, that gets resolved over time, but there's going to be a lag effect as the administration works through the regulatory process to accomplish what their objectives are on GHG. So when we purchase credits, we amortize them over the time -- the remaining life of those credits. Paul Jacobson: Executive VP & CFO Yes. Well, Mark, thanks for hanging on for the whole call. I appreciate you get your last question. The Super Cruise revenue is a couple of things. So remember, when we sell a vehicle with Super Cruise, we include 3 years of prepaid services on that. So that balance then amortizes over a 3-year period. So what you're seeing is growth in those initial rates as we ramp up production and sales of vehicles equipped with Super Cruise. The second aspect of it, which we're continuing to see really good penetration and attachment rates is on the renewal. So at the end of 3 years, customers are approached with would they like to subscribe. And we've seen attachment rates in the low 40% range with people stepping up and renewing that. So that's where you're seeing a lot of the growth in Super Cruise. In OnStar, we include an OnStar basics package with the sale of vehicles that has -- that amortizes over the life of that period. But it also -- what it does is gives us an engagement opportunity with the consumer that is really laying the foundation for, number one, enhanced OnStar services currently, but also then second, you look at GM rewards, you look at opportunities when we get software-defined vehicles down the road. It's really a big step function. So that's where you're seeing a lot of the deferred revenue growing and coming in at very attractive software-like margins.**Paul Jacobson:** ë„¤, Mark, í†µí™” ëê¹Œì§€ í•¨ê»˜í•´ ì£¼ì…”ì„œ ê°ì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë§ˆì§€ë§‰ ì§ˆë¬¸ ì£¼ì…”ì„œ ê³ ë§™ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ìŠˆí¼ í¬ë£¨ì¦ˆ ë§¤ì¶œì€ ëª‡ ê°€ì§€ ìš”ì†Œë¡œ êµ¬ì„±ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ìŠˆí¼ í¬ë£¨ì¦ˆê°€ ì¥ì°©ëœ ì°¨ëŸ‰ì„ íŒë§¤í•  ë•Œ 3ë…„ê°„ì˜ ì„ ë¶ˆ ì„œë¹„ìŠ¤ê°€ í¬í•¨ëœë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì„ ê¸°ì–µí•˜ì…”ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ê·¸ë˜ì„œ ê·¸ ì”ì•¡ì´ 3ë…„ì— ê±¸ì³ ìƒê°ë˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. í˜„ì¬ ë³´ì‹œëŠ” ê²ƒì€ ìŠˆí¼ í¬ë£¨ì¦ˆ ì¥ì°© ì°¨ëŸ‰ì˜ ìƒì‚°ê³¼ íŒë§¤ê°€ ì¦ê°€í•˜ë©´ì„œ ì´ˆê¸° ë¹„ìœ¨ì´ ì„±ì¥í•˜ê³  ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ê²ƒì…ë‹ˆë‹¤.

Chairman & CEO: Well, I think the number of vehicles that we launched this year, the new energy vehicles, I think, are doing very well, over 50% as we indicated with the right software, the right technology. And virtually across the board, we have in China for China solutions that I think are resonating really well in the marketplace. And I think that discipline, along with the discipline in the way the business is operating of making sure we manage inventory, which allows us to manage incentives. And it also has allowed us to have a much better relationship with the dealers because we've had a dramatic improvement in their profitability. So I think it's -- if you want to say what's going to drive China's business overall, it's the right product portfolio and then the discipline in which we're managing the business. # GM Q4 2025 Earnings Call Summary

## Key Financial Metrics & Guidance

- **2026 Guidance**: EBIT of $14 billion (midpoint); North America margins expected to return to 8-10% range
- **Pricing**: Flat to slightly up in 2026, reflecting annualization of MY2026 pricing with no new increases assumed
- **Tariff Impact**: $3-4 billion gross tariff costs assumed (using 15% South Korea rate); expect 40%+ offset through self-help measures, resulting in lower net tariffs vs. 2025
- **Headwinds**: $1-1.5 billion from commodities, DRAM chips, and FX; $1-1.5 billion in onshoring/software expenses (split roughly 50/50)
- **Tailwinds**: $1 billion warranty cost improvement; $500-750 million regulatory/compliance credit savings; improved EV profitability

## Strategic Developments

- **Product Portfolio**: Maintaining dedicated EV platform while adding hybrids in key segments; new full-size truck launch expected later in 2026 (with associated production downtime)
- **Technology**: Super Cruise revenue growing to $400M in 2026 (from $234M in 2025) with ~40% renewal rates; next-gen software-defined vehicle platform on track for 2028 with eyes-off/hands-off capability
- **China Turnaround**: Sustained profitability expected through new energy vehicles (50%+ of portfolio), improved dealer relationships, and operational discipline
- **GM Financial**: Industrial Bank conditional approval provides new funding source to reduce cost of capital

## Management Tone & Risks

**Tone**: Confident and disciplined. Management emphasized operational resilience, product strength, and ability to navigate uncertainty while maintaining margin targets.

**Key Risks**:
- EV demand uncertainty following tax credit elimination (steady-state demand unclear)
- Potential South Korea tariff increase from 15% to 25%
- Memory chip supply/pricing pressures
- Ongoing V8 engine warranty investigation
- Chinese OEM competition in international markets

**Strengths**: Strong inventory discipline (48
